<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer7086289357547915105"><strong>Four women-four friends-share a determination to stop a killer who has been stalking newlyweds in San Francisco. Each one holds a piece of the puzzle: Lindsay Boxer is a homicide inspector in the San Francisco Police Department, Claire Washburn is a medical examiner, Jill Bernhardt is an assistant D.A., and Cindy Thomas just started working the crime desk of the San Franci</strong></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7086289357547915105"><strong>Four women-four friends-share a determination to stop a killer who has been stalking newlyweds in San Francisco. Each one holds a piece of the puzzle: Lindsay Boxer is a homicide inspector in the San Francisco Police Department, Claire Washburn is a medical examiner, Jill Bernhardt is an assistant D.A., and Cindy Thomas just started working the crime desk of the San Francisco Chronicle.<br /><br />But the usual procedures aren't bringing them any closer to stopping the killings. So these women form a Women's Murder Club to collaborate outside the box and pursue the case by sidestepping their bosses and giving one another a hand.<br /><br />The four women develop intense bonds as they pursue a killer whose crimes have stunned an entire city. Working together, they track down the most terrifying and unexpected killer they have ever encountered-before a shocking conclusion in which everything they knew turns out to be devastatingly wrong.</strong></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7086289357547915105">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/12719417?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 21, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/793275-zach" class="user" title="Zach">Zach</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13137.1st_to_Die" title="Paperback 9780446696616" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">almost nobody</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Zach by: </span>
      my mom
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/793275-zach?shelf=stupid-books" class="actionLinkLite">stupid-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer12719417">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4000027729693133051">How in the world is he a best-selling author? His characters are shallow, his writing is mediocre, and when he writes about romance it feels mechanical and formulaic. This book had a twist at the end, but it was the worst sort of twist - the kind that you can't really predict because he probably didn't think to add it until after the book was already written - leaving out any traces of foreshadowing. I haven't read any of his other books and don't plan to now. When you have as little time for le</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4000027729693133051">How in the world is he a best-selling author? His characters are shallow, his writing is mediocre, and when he writes about romance it feels mechanical and formulaic. This book had a twist at the end, but it was the worst sort of twist - the kind that you can't really predict because he probably didn't think to add it until after the book was already written - leaving out any traces of foreshadowing. I haven't read any of his other books and don't plan to now. When you have as little time for leisure reading as I do, you waste as little time as possible reading crap.<br /><br />Also, he uses too much vulgarity and too much sex. It isn't even romantic sex; it's cheap.<br /><br />I recommend this book only to people who have already read every other book in the world and would rather read something they haven't read then reread a good book.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4000027729693133051">...more</a>

          </span>

  <a href="/user/show/47212-the-book-maven" class="left imgcol" title="The Book Maven"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1178140714p2/47212.jpg" alt="The Book Maven" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/18013676?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 29, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/47212-the-book-maven" class="user" title="The Book Maven">The Book Maven</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13137.1st_to_Die" title="Paperback 9780446696616" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/47212-the-book-maven?shelf=read-mystery" class="actionLinkLite">read-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer18013676">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer778199190070886985">Am I the only one that thinks that "Women's Murder Club" sounds not only hokey but juvenile and begging mockery?<br /><br />The story: a psycho serial killer begins murdering newly married couples. 4 women, each with their own stake in cracking the case, are determined to nail the killer, and so band together outside of official channels to pool their resources and figure it all out. There is a red herring (if one could call it that) and a vaguely surprising twist at the end, but I read this with an unusual</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText778199190070886985">Am I the only one that thinks that "Women's Murder Club" sounds not only hokey but juvenile and begging mockery?<br /><br />The story: a psycho serial killer begins murdering newly married couples. 4 women, each with their own stake in cracking the case, are determined to nail the killer, and so band together outside of official channels to pool their resources and figure it all out. There is a red herring (if one could call it that) and a vaguely surprising twist at the end, but I read this with an unusual level of detachment and disinterest, and so was not impressed by anything.<br /><br />I just wasn't hugely impressed with this book. Patterson's handling of the female characters and their relationships with each other were stilted, forced, and lacked nuance from beginning to end. I get the impression that Patterson does not truly grasp how women operate, and how their relationships develop.<br /><br />As for the plot itself, well, it was vaguely diverting, but not much more. <br /><br />The only halfway compelling facet of this mystery was the main character's struggle with an illness of which she has just learned; an illness that is potentially fatal, can advance rapidly (and in fact does), and that begins to make her realize her own sense of mortality, and how time might be running out. <br /><br />I love books in which the female characters are young, put-together, strong, successful...I think what is the most disappointing about this book is that there is SO MUCH unrealized potential. Grrrr.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="778199190070886985">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/59523-lydia" class="user" title="Lydia">Lydia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13137.1st_to_Die" title="Paperback 9780446696616" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Mystery/ Thriller/ Suspense Lovers</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/59523-lydia?shelf=mystery-thriller-suspense" class="actionLinkLite">mystery-thriller-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer16088118">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10082317012493889945">This is my first Patterson experience. The book was quite captivating and enthralling.There are half a million detective-serial killer novels out there... Patterson's are by far near if not at the top of the list! His chapters are so brisk you'll find your self half-way through the book before you know it. As well, the suspense is so well paced, and he also tosses in so many possibilities and clues to murderer's identity into the mix, there's no way you'll be able to set the book down until you</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10082317012493889945">This is my first Patterson experience. The book was quite captivating and enthralling.There are half a million detective-serial killer novels out there... Patterson's are by far near if not at the top of the list! His chapters are so brisk you'll find your self half-way through the book before you know it. As well, the suspense is so well paced, and he also tosses in so many possibilities and clues to murderer's identity into the mix, there's no way you'll be able to set the book down until you have reached the finale. In addition to top-notch suspense, Patterson gives deep insight into the minds of our four heroine's, we know their dark secrets , and sympathize with them (especially Linday with the rare blood disorder, an original sub-plot)therefore we truly care about what happens to them. And as you approach the end of Patterson's 1st to Die, you breath of sigh of relief, only until the last page where Patterson chucks another twist at you, you nearly fall out of your seat in cardiac arrest! Never have I read a novel with a final twist so near the end of the book I can't help but applaud Patterson for being so clever. Reading it was like driving a car, through beautiful countryside relaxing and enjoying it- UNTIL you suddenly see the road sink below the horizon realizing your approaching a cliff at rapid speed! Kudos to Patterson, this book Thrills!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10082317012493889945">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/353707-diane" class="user" title="Diane">Diane</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who likes James Patterson</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer9667836">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7898059262537454626">My impulse as I read 1st to Die was to start editing. Overwriting, reduncancy, and sentimentality took the place of plot structure, character development, and freshness. Each of the four women was described in terms of her profession and ethnic background--sassy Black woman medical examiner with a faithful musician husband, sleek, sophisticated put-upon woman DA who gets no respect from her male superiors, perky newspaper reporter whose risk-taking allows her to get the scoops that more seasoned</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7898059262537454626">My impulse as I read 1st to Die was to start editing. Overwriting, reduncancy, and sentimentality took the place of plot structure, character development, and freshness. Each of the four women was described in terms of her profession and ethnic background--sassy Black woman medical examiner with a faithful musician husband, sleek, sophisticated put-upon woman DA who gets no respect from her male superiors, perky newspaper reporter whose risk-taking allows her to get the scoops that more seasoned newspaper people are afraid to go after, and, of course, our depressed, troubled, obsessed main character who gets her life back just to lose everything and speaks in cliches throughout the narrative. <br /><br />This book was a fast read, but I won't bother reading any of the other books in the series. I wonder if the TV show is any better? If so, it's only because some decent writers turned the script into something better than this book.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7898059262537454626">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer9391417344237690470">I was curious about this series because it's obviously very popular, but I can't say I'm terribly impressed by it. First of all, the sappy "you go girl" female characters didn't seem very true to life to me. Patterson seems to think that name-checking Sarah McLachlan and Tori Amos, plus a lot of hugging and randomly saying "I love you, girl", means he has created believable female characters. Not so much. <br /><br />Also, I thought the plot was melodramatic, and the continual twists were more tedious than</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9391417344237690470">I was curious about this series because it's obviously very popular, but I can't say I'm terribly impressed by it. First of all, the sappy "you go girl" female characters didn't seem very true to life to me. Patterson seems to think that name-checking Sarah McLachlan and Tori Amos, plus a lot of hugging and randomly saying "I love you, girl", means he has created believable female characters. Not so much. <br /><br />Also, I thought the plot was melodramatic, and the continual twists were more tedious than shocking or surprising. </span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/33387110" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/113627-joyce" class="left imgcol" title="Joyce"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1273954824p2/113627.jpg" alt="Joyce" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/33387110?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 04, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/113627-joyce" class="user" title="Joyce">Joyce</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13137.1st_to_Die" title="Paperback 9780446696616" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer33387110">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7031956581226177970">There's nothing specifically GOOD about this book, but damned if the pages don't practically turn themselves. It's pure junk food, and I mean that as a compliment insofar as processed food is very highly engineered by very skilled workers to be universally appealing to the widest possible market.<br /><br />Patterson -- a top advertising exec before his writing career -- seems to have decided that in addition to his bestselling Alex Cross novels and film adaptations, he needed a series that appealed to wome</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7031956581226177970">There's nothing specifically GOOD about this book, but damned if the pages don't practically turn themselves. It's pure junk food, and I mean that as a compliment insofar as processed food is very highly engineered by very skilled workers to be universally appealing to the widest possible market.<br /><br />Patterson -- a top advertising exec before his writing career -- seems to have decided that in addition to his bestselling Alex Cross novels and film adaptations, he needed a series that appealed to women and television. Four chicks with different skills -- ensemble cast! Alex Cross works on the East Coast, so we'll set this series on the West Coast! They have complicated love lives and health problems and career setbacks for background color!<br /><br />It's a sign of Patterson's professionalism that he doesn't make you feel like a market segment while you're actually reading. He wants to tell a good story, and shows real interest in his characters' feelings no matter how banal. I doubt I'll be reading another entry in this series, but new writers could do a lot worse than following this craftsman's lead.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7031956581226177970">...more</a>

          </span>

  <a href="/user/show/414610-heidi" class="left imgcol" title="Heidi"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1190698859p2/414610.jpg" alt="Heidi" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/42131826?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 06, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/414610-heidi" class="user" title="Heidi">Heidi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13137.1st_to_Die" title="Paperback 9780446696616" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/414610-heidi?shelf=2009-reads" class="actionLinkLite">2009-reads</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/414610-heidi?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer42131826">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5679621282991739788">I’ve been having trouble concentrating enough to read anything involving thought and effort so mindless mysteries/thrillers are just what the doctor ordered. This one, though? No thanks.<br /><br />By page 45 I decided I hated James Patterson writing women. The head of the homicide division and the chief medical examiner of San Francisco are disgusted, sickened, and “have to turn away” from a body. What atrocity can these two strong, experienced, professional women not handle? A body with a single stab woun</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5679621282991739788">I’ve been having trouble concentrating enough to read anything involving thought and effort so mindless mysteries/thrillers are just what the doctor ordered. This one, though? No thanks.<br /><br />By page 45 I decided I hated James Patterson writing women. The head of the homicide division and the chief medical examiner of San Francisco are disgusted, sickened, and “have to turn away” from a body. What atrocity can these two strong, experienced, professional women not handle? A body with a single stab wound. What?! Oh, but the male detective? He’s just fine! He even steps in to offer our lead homicide investigator an arm to lean on! Seriously? You’ve got to be kidding me.<br /><br />I found the interactions between the female friends not realistic in the slightest. I actually snorted with laughter a few times at how ridiculous and cliché they were. <br /><br />Overall I found the writing to be stilted and not especially engaging. I can’t say I enjoyed it much at all. And I don’t normally notice these things but the man used the word, “chilling” so many times that, not only did I notice, but was really annoyed by it. Good writers don’t need to tell their readers how to react to their writing. I should find your descriptions “chilling” without being told to over and over and over again.<br /><br />And my most petty complaint: The Women’s Murder Club. Four intelligent, urbane professionals and that’s the name of their group? Couldn’t he have come up with a name that wasn’t so hackneyed and immature? It might as well be The Four Females Who Find Killers Club or The Four Awesome Chicks Hunting Bad Guys Club. Would a homicide investigator, coroner, prosecutor, and reporter who were male have to create a “club” and name it something so hokey? Again, I think it goes back to Patterson’s inability to write women with any realism or truth. And his desire to create a series and characters that could easily be marketed and turned into a movie and/or TV show. <br /><br />I enjoy gruesome, bloody thrillers but really doubt I can bring myself to skim through the rest of these books based solely on how poorly written I find the characters.<br /><br />ETA: I just found out that James Patterson earned $50 million from June 2007 to June 2008. No, that’s not a typo. I’m equal parts horrified and inspired to write something that my biggest fans will excitedly describe as a “quick and easy read.”</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5679621282991739788">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_414292262">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/414292262" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1336988-wendy" class="left imgcol" title="Wendy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1296003715p2/1336988.jpg" alt="Wendy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/414292262?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 14, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1336988-wendy" class="user" title="Wendy">Wendy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13137.1st_to_Die" title="Paperback 9780446696616" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer414292262">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4333129905470243881">I believe this will be the last James Patterson novel that I read. It was another of his titles with cardboard characters, stilted dialogue, and a plot with unlikely but convenient and contrived coincidences, which all equal a very thin read. <br /><br />In this book, the women's "friendship" came across as canned and forced. I think the characters were developed solely on a quota system for just the perfect mix that could solve murders. It was almost as if I could hear him thinking, "Hmmm...let's see...I n</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4333129905470243881">I believe this will be the last James Patterson novel that I read. It was another of his titles with cardboard characters, stilted dialogue, and a plot with unlikely but convenient and contrived coincidences, which all equal a very thin read. <br /><br />In this book, the women's "friendship" came across as canned and forced. I think the characters were developed solely on a quota system for just the perfect mix that could solve murders. It was almost as if I could hear him thinking, "Hmmm...let's see...I need a homicide detective (check), a medical examiner (check), and oh, maybe a reporter (check again). What else? Yes, of course! A district attorney too! (final check). Let's also make sure I represent the independent tough woman working in a man's world, the ethnic woman, the up-and-comer with moxie, and the uber-professional careerist. Done and done." <br /><br />Perhaps his use of ghostwriters who write stories about characters they didn't envision doing things that someone else has imagined and outlined is what causes this flatness. Whatever the reason, the end result just isn't for me. <br /><br />While I admire James Patterson's apparent marketing genius and entrepreneurial spirit in creating book outlines and farming out the actual storytelling and writing to other authors, he is now really just a brand cranking out books at breakneck speed. But at least he's honest about it. And he's right that his writing/outlines do appeal to a certain type of reader who wants a fast-paced read that doesn't require heavy lifting. Nothing wrong with that, but I'll be moving on.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4333129905470243881">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13137.1st_to_Die" title="Paperback 9780446696616" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who likes suspense/thrillers/mysteries</span></div>

        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer26472930">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9834745976028331491">Wow! This book was great! I almost gave it 4-stars, as there are some subplot development issues (the main character, Lindsay, developed well as a character, but has a lot of things that happen out of the main plot that do not directly relate, but don't exactly take away - Patterson is trying to add more emotional, real-life appeal to the novel). Overall I loved it!<br /><br />The book has a lot of suspense is a very quick read! Lindsay is trying to catch a "bride and groom" pyschopath killer while dealing</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9834745976028331491">Wow! This book was great! I almost gave it 4-stars, as there are some subplot development issues (the main character, Lindsay, developed well as a character, but has a lot of things that happen out of the main plot that do not directly relate, but don't exactly take away - Patterson is trying to add more emotional, real-life appeal to the novel). Overall I loved it!<br /><br />The book has a lot of suspense is a very quick read! Lindsay is trying to catch a "bride and groom" pyschopath killer while dealing with issues of life. She and three other girlfriends form a club - The Women's Murder Club - so they can solve the murders together, off the record, and as a "girls-only" atmosphere to alleviate the male dominated professions each woman is involved in. Lindsay is a senior inspector for the San Fransico PD, Cliare is the Assistant Medical Examiner, Cindy is a rookie reporter, and Jill is the Assistant District Attorney. These women come together and make real friendships as they each help each other's case, career, and life.<br /><br />3/4 of the way into it I thought I had figured it out. Well nearly every chapter after turned the book into a corkscrew - twist after twist after twist. It did not take away from the book because you kept guessing! I was so close... Then, the ending is - killer.<br /><br />Read it and continue on into the next books in the series!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9834745976028331491">...more</a>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer135609028">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1296955570980819402"><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://photobucket.com/images/womens%20murder%20club"> <img class="escapedImg" alt="Womens Murder Club Pictures, Images and Photos" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380342687i/698415.jpg" /></a><br /><br />It is really hard to rate this book since it seems that this is a mix of cheesiness and cliche but it is also unpredictable and thrilling. It has some terrible parts but there are also amazing parts.<br /><br /><strong>Pros:</strong><br />1. I love the title 1st to die and my assumption to who will be the "1st to die" is wrong so I guess that is a plus point for the book.<br /><br />2. I really like the murder scenes it is very grotesquely describe that it made me shiver just imagining them.<br /><br />3. The twist in the end about who's the true murde</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1296955570980819402"><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://photobucket.com/images/womens%20murder%20club">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt="Womens Murder Club Pictures, Images and Photos" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380342687i/698415.jpg" /></a><br /><br />It is really hard to rate this book since it seems that this is a mix of cheesiness and cliche but it is also unpredictable and thrilling. It has some terrible parts but there are also amazing parts.<br /><br /><strong>Pros:</strong><br />1. I love the title 1st to die and my assumption to who will be the "1st to die" is wrong so I guess that is a plus point for the book.<br /><br />2. I really like the murder scenes it is very grotesquely describe that it made me shiver just imagining them.<br /><br />3. The twist in the end about who's the true murderer is something that I totally didn't see coming and I think it is a great twist, very shocking indeed.<br /><br />4. Even the epilogue of the book is exhilarating, I thought it is all over but there's still some heart-stopping action at the epilogue of the book. <br /><br /><strong>Cons:</strong><br />1. The characters and their relationships felt very awkward and contrived for me. The dialogues are very cheesy that it actually made me gag a couple of times.<br /><br />2. Even the Women's Murder Club thingy felt a little bit push, it is just there for the sake of a bad ass title for the series but it is really lazily written. The parts wherein they're talking or even when they first met each other is very unnatural. They're like BFF's all of a sudden.<br /><br />3. Lindsay's "blood disease" is a little bit cliche even the coughing of the blood part.<br /><blockquote>"I coughed a raw, burning stinging in my chest, then I shook and coughed some more. Gradually, I felt the spell recede. I took a breath, opened my eyes. I shuddered. There was blood all over the sink."</blockquote><br />--What I mean is that this is really cliche when you watch those drama series on tv, you'll always have this scene.<br /><br />4. The romance is a bit cheesy too, especially at the beginning of the book. Even their first night together is written in a very cheesy way it just made me puke.<br /><br /><br />5. Also another thing that pisses me off is how the chapters are really short and guess what this book has a total of 126 chapters and one epilogue. I am so not kidding.<br /><br />6. Here we go again with James Patterson's ridiculous deux ex machina. This is not my first J. Patterson book and I've read the first two books in his Maximum Ride Series and that's what I notice about both of these books is that he uses deux ex machina all the time to just move his plot.<br /><br />Like for example in this book, Jenks was inside the van and he is there because he's already a prisoner and then he have these handcuffs and some police who were watching for him etc. Then a GOD DAMN EARTHQUAKE came and he's free. I mean come on James Patterson this is just too convenient isn't it? <br /><br />Okay ranting over, all and all I did enjoy this book and I really am grateful that someone from The Filipino Group here in Goodreads gave this book to me last December. Though now I'm not sure who's the original owner since I just pick it up on the giveaway pile. Nevertheless thank you whoever you may be :).</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_27220589">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27220589" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1313252-larisa" class="left imgcol" title="Larisa"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1215635829p2/1313252.jpg" alt="Larisa" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/27220589?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 14, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1313252-larisa" class="user" title="Larisa">Larisa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13137.1st_to_Die" title="Paperback 9780446696616" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1313252-larisa?shelf=book-club-picks" class="actionLinkLite">book-club-picks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer27220589'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer27220589">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14696117314726963455">This was my first James Patterson novel, and I have to say it was probably my last. I was expecting much, much more from a best-selling author - more complexity, more depth, more emotion. <br /><br />While I can see how the plot lends itself well to summer movie adaptation, as has been Patterson's style in the past with <u>Kiss the Girls</u> and <u>Along Came a Spider</u>, I found the writing entirely too simplistic, as if were distilled down to appeal to the lowest common denominator. Nothing too challenging so as not t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14696117314726963455">This was my first James Patterson novel, and I have to say it was probably my last. I was expecting much, much more from a best-selling author - more complexity, more depth, more emotion. <br /><br />While I can see how the plot lends itself well to summer movie adaptation, as has been Patterson's style in the past with <u>Kiss the Girls</u> and <u>Along Came a Spider</u>, I found the writing entirely too simplistic, as if were distilled down to appeal to the lowest common denominator. Nothing too challenging so as not to offend the masses. The characters were flat. The love affair.. Don't get me started. Let's just say that you could totally tell that a man wrote this book. The two main detectives jumped from begrudging partners to passionate lovers with a blink of an eye and little to no development, which annoyed me. The ending - a disjointed killer-surprise-attack-for-one-final-bloody-act kind of deal. Eh...<br /><br />I would recommend this book to someone who just wants a quick read for a plane trip, someone seeking a cheap &amp; dirty thrill but not much else. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14696117314726963455">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_111051448">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111051448" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light" class="left imgcol" title="Crystal Starr Light"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1435785327p2/3990525.jpg" alt="Crystal Starr Light" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/111051448?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 13, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light" class="user" title="Crystal Starr Light">Crystal Starr Light</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13137.1st_to_Die" title="Paperback 9780446696616" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=read-at-your-own-risk" class="actionLinkLite">read-at-your-own-risk</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=idiot-protagonist" class="actionLinkLite">idiot-protagonist</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer111051448">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11653975503043160695">It has been some time since I have read any mystery novels, so after much hunting through bookstores, I eagerly picked up the New York Bestselling book, 1st to Die.<br /><br />The beginning had me hooked. Looking through the eyes of the criminal-and the eyes of his soon-to-be victims-was awesome. I started out liking Lindsay, Cindy, and Claire. Lindsay's medical condition helped me grow closer to her (which I found slightly surprising). And as a public transportation rider, I enjoyed the short chapters. But</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11653975503043160695">It has been some time since I have read any mystery novels, so after much hunting through bookstores, I eagerly picked up the New York Bestselling book, 1st to Die.<br /><br />The beginning had me hooked. Looking through the eyes of the criminal-and the eyes of his soon-to-be victims-was awesome. I started out liking Lindsay, Cindy, and Claire. Lindsay's medical condition helped me grow closer to her (which I found slightly surprising). And as a public transportation rider, I enjoyed the short chapters. But as time progressed, the following began to annoy me:<br /><br />1. Through most of the book, I had a hard time thinking of Lindsay as a woman. It just felt like a guy writing what he thought a woman might think!<br /><br />2. I don't see why Patterson bothered to call this a Women's Murder Mystery Club adventure. Almost the entire book centers on Lindsay and her point of view. Cindy has only two major sequences where she does anything of any consequence. Claire is only given one section to herself. Mostly, she appears only when Lindsay consults her. And I don't understand why Jill was brought up at all-her role was completely meaningless.<br /><br />3. The formation of the club is something I would expect from a young adult novel. One minute, the women go out for drinks, the next, they are bragging about having sex and where they have tattoos (yes, this is exactly what I do when I just meet a new group of women!). And what do the four really do to solve the mystery? I don't see how they helped Lindsay out much at all.<br /><br />4. Lindsay and Chris were a cute couple, but their romance went way too fast. They started off okay, and then suddenly, they were in bed with each other. Their chemistry was thrown together hastily and more "telling" than "showing".<br /><br />5. Once the last couple is killed, I feel that there is no more reason to be invested in the story. It's almost as though Patterson said, "I've killed the last couple now." I would really have preferred him to allude to a fourth murder, and for Lindsay and Chris to rush to the rescue.<br /><br />I was really looking forward to reading this book and was sorry to see it continue to fall below my expectations as each page progressed. As soon as I finished it, I took it to a bookstore and traded it in for something else. I really would like to give Patterson a second chance-perhaps some of his earlier works-but after this novel, I am a little more wary about how I spend my $8.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11653975503043160695">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_112119777">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112119777" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2850786-jennifer" class="left imgcol" title="Jennifer"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1443208538p2/2850786.jpg" alt="Jennifer" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/112119777?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 17, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2850786-jennifer" class="user" title="Jennifer">Jennifer</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13137.1st_to_Die" title="Paperback 9780446696616" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2850786-jennifer?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer112119777">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9733191842417901995">I loved 1st to Die. It was the perfect beginning to a thrilling series. I thought the women's decision to join forces and work together to stop a serial killer was ingenious. I think it spoke to the true character of each of them, showing that their true goal was to protect the public from danger rather than be recognized personally for being the sole reason the killer was stopped.<br /><br />The book works so well because of the differences each woman brings to the table. Lindsey works well as a main chara</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9733191842417901995">I loved 1st to Die. It was the perfect beginning to a thrilling series. I thought the women's decision to join forces and work together to stop a serial killer was ingenious. I think it spoke to the true character of each of them, showing that their true goal was to protect the public from danger rather than be recognized personally for being the sole reason the killer was stopped.<br /><br />The book works so well because of the differences each woman brings to the table. Lindsey works well as a main character because of the other women in her life. Had the book been Lindsey on her own, I don't think it would have been nearly as enjoyable.<br /><br />1st to Die was a wonderful mystery that didn't hold back. The murders were shocking. The serial killer was targeting couples on their wedding nights. Just the concept alone is upsetting. The frenzied race to find the killer was easily felt and I found myself caught up in the momentum of the book. Once started, I couldn't put it down. I had to know who the killer was and how they would be stopped.<br /><br />The first book in any mystery series can be hit or miss due to the necessity of laying groundwork and introducing background information. 1st to Die was definitely a hit for me. I honestly can't think of one thing that wasn't perfect in this book. If you haven't started this series yet, you are missing out.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9733191842417901995">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_63224538">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63224538" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/991905-rose" class="left imgcol" title="Rose"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1209050240p2/991905.jpg" alt="Rose" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/63224538?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 12, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/991905-rose" class="user" title="Rose">Rose</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6283575-1st-to-die" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer63224538">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15137035876963009308">The gruesome murder of a newlywed couple just hours after their wedding ceremony shocks the city of San Francisco. What's more, it seems the murderer is on a bit of spree! Enter Detective Lindsay Boxer - a tenacious go-getter who throws herself into this high-profile case as a distraction from her personal struggles. Her best friend and confidante? Claire, the smart and sophisticated county medical examiner. Then there's Cindy, a determined young reporter who's ingenuity and good luck land her t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15137035876963009308">The gruesome murder of a newlywed couple just hours after their wedding ceremony shocks the city of San Francisco. What's more, it seems the murderer is on a bit of spree! Enter Detective Lindsay Boxer - a tenacious go-getter who throws herself into this high-profile case as a distraction from her personal struggles. Her best friend and confidante? Claire, the smart and sophisticated county medical examiner. Then there's Cindy, a determined young reporter who's ingenuity and good luck land her the biggest case of her fledgling career. And don't forget Jill, the assistant DA whose character is a bit of an afterthought, but is nevertheless important since she makes up the fourth member of the Women's Murder Club. Together the women decide to cut through the bureaucracy and pool their resources to solve the crimes... before the murderer can strike again!<br /><br />The book is one giant cliche, featuring four female characters each with as much depth as an inflatable kiddie pool. The romantic lead, one Chris Raleigh, couldn't have been more dull. A police big-shot who specializes in public relations, he's sent in to replace Lindsay's gruff and tough partner (Jacobi) due to the highly sensitive and public nature of the case. Instead of taking over, Raleigh presents with a relaxed and helpful demeanor, which naturally throws Lindsay for a loop (despite her reputation for being highly observant and possessing a keen ability to read people). Oh she's irritated about the situation alright, but, of course, finds herself slowly falling for him. Add to that her unwillingness to deal with an unexpected personal crisis, and Patterson has colored in a paint-by-numbers picture of a tough-on-the-outside, gooey-on-the-inside struggling female cop. Classic. <br /><br />The plot was okay, but not particularly inventive. Typically I do not like when mysteries vacillate between the detective's and the killer's perspectives, but I will say that this story's shifting points of view added some much-needed suspense. In fairness, 1st to Die is a first book, so Patterson will have ample time to develop his characters over what is sure to be a lengthy series (already eight books and counting). I, however, do not intend to find out personally how successful he is.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15137035876963009308">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_60394072">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/60394072" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1242515-hannah" class="left imgcol" title="Hannah"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1346493023p2/1242515.jpg" alt="Hannah" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/60394072?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 20, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1242515-hannah" class="user" title="Hannah">Hannah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13137.1st_to_Die" title="Paperback 9780446696616" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1242515-hannah?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer60394072">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7221453031895593447">I found the way the actual murders were carried out rather chilling, and the short, curt delivery helped develop that atmosphere. Although it was fairly easy to guess who the murderer was going to be after about halfway, the tension never eased until it reached the climax. The characters were also reasonably interesting, although their interactions always felt somewhat fake and stiff. Patterson <em>tells</em> me they're friends, but I don't see it.<br /><br />However, the real letdown for me was James Patterson's wr</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7221453031895593447">I found the way the actual murders were carried out rather chilling, and the short, curt delivery helped develop that atmosphere. Although it was fairly easy to guess who the murderer was going to be after about halfway, the tension never eased until it reached the climax. The characters were also reasonably interesting, although their interactions always felt somewhat fake and stiff. Patterson <em>tells</em> me they're friends, but I don't see it.<br /><br />However, the real letdown for me was James Patterson's writing. The man obviously has some decent stories up his sleeves, but the one thing that never changes is the fact that he can't write for beans. His editor's obviously not earning his/her pay either, because the very first sentence in the novel was probably one of the most jarring and badly phrased beginnings I've ever had the misfortune to read. The fact that he chose to present the story in first person didn't help, because it's very hard to pull off a great first person perspective without sounding clunky, even for the best of authors.<br /><br />Also, I found issues with the flow of the story. Again, the first chapter was particularly bad, as was the epilogue. They stuck out, and I couldn't seem to connect them very well with the rest of the story. Where were they supposed to tie in? I may never have found out if I hadn't read a good review that interpreted it satisfactorily. The ending was also a bit of a stunner, and the death moved by so quickly that it was almost surreal. I found that rather anticlimatic. A character that was built up to be Lindsay's new companion all through the novel was gone just like that, and I found myself wondering what was the point of him being there at all, except to make Lindsay look even more tragic.<br /><br />A good writer James Patterson is not, but if you read fast enough, all is forgiven because the plot moves along rather snappily.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7221453031895593447">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2965534942823091189">"First in the series of the Women’s Murder Club The Women's Murder Club pits four San Francisco women professionals against a serial killer who's stalking and murdering newlyweds in bestselling author James Patterson's newest thriller.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText2965534942823091189">"First in the series of the Women’s Murder Club The Women's Murder Club pits four San Francisco women professionals against a serial killer who's stalking and murdering newlyweds in bestselling author James Patterson's newest thriller. Lindsay Boxer is a homicide inspector who's just gotten some very bad news (a life threatening blood disease). She deals with it by immersing herself in her newest case and soliciting the personal as well as professional support of her closest friend, who happens to be the city's medical examiner. The two women, along with an ambitious and sympathetic reporter and an assistant DA, form an unlikely alliance, pooling their information and bypassing the chain of command in an engaging, suspenseful story whose gruesome setup is vintage Patterson." <br /><br />This was the 2nd Patterson book I have read. It was pretty good. The team of women is an interesting concept. Patterson does a pretty good job with it.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Law &amp; Order and CSI fans</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer14870382">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3448214307333006159">It's probably not fair for me to rate this book. It's really not my style. I didn't get more than 50 pages into it. I find that I empathize with the characters too much these days. That makes it very difficult to read a book like this. To explain, the book starts out with the main character trying to kill herself, then gives us a happy intro to the first victims in the story, and moves on to the point of view of the murderer as he kills those first victims. He thinks to himself, what is the wors</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3448214307333006159">It's probably not fair for me to rate this book. It's really not my style. I didn't get more than 50 pages into it. I find that I empathize with the characters too much these days. That makes it very difficult to read a book like this. To explain, the book starts out with the main character trying to kill herself, then gives us a happy intro to the first victims in the story, and moves on to the point of view of the murderer as he kills those first victims. He thinks to himself, what is the worst thing he could do? And then he does it. And I'm sure that for some, this is entertaining. But for me, it's just disturbing and something I can't get out of my head. I'm sure the point is that later, there will be mystery and suspense, and the murderer will get caught and all will be well - I just don't care to get there. I read for fun, and heart-wrenching, disgusting, horrible murders aren't fun. IMO.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/885577599?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 30, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/26984061-tammie-tackett" class="user" title="Tammie Tackett">Tammie Tackett</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13137.1st_to_Die" title="Paperback 9780446696616" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/26984061-tammie-tackett?shelf=my-reading-challenge-for-2016" class="actionLinkLite">my-reading-challenge-for-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer885577599">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2628967004897774756">This is my first Patterson experience. The book was quite captivating and enthralling.There are half a million detective-serial killer novels out there... Patterson's are by far near if not at the top of the list! His chapters are so brisk you'll find your self half-way through the book before you know it. As well, the suspense is so well paced, and he also tosses in so many possibilities and clues to murderer's identity into the mix, there's no way you'll be able to set the book down until you</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2628967004897774756">This is my first Patterson experience. The book was quite captivating and enthralling.There are half a million detective-serial killer novels out there... Patterson's are by far near if not at the top of the list! His chapters are so brisk you'll find your self half-way through the book before you know it. As well, the suspense is so well paced, and he also tosses in so many possibilities and clues to murderer's identity into the mix, there's no way you'll be able to set the book down until you have reached the finale. In addition to top-notch suspense, Patterson gives deep insight into the minds of our four heroine's, we know their dark secrets , and sympathize with them (especially Linday with the rare blood disorder, an original sub-plot)therefore we truly care about what happens to them. And as you approach the end of Patterson's 1st to Die, you breath of sigh of relief, only until the last page where Patterson chucks another twist at you, you nearly fall out of your seat in cardiac arrest! Never have I read a novel with a final twist so near the end of the book I can't help but applaud Patterson for being so clever. Reading it was like driving a car, through beautiful countryside relaxing and enjoying it- UNTIL you suddenly see the road sink below the horizon realizing your approaching a cliff at rapid speed! Kudos to Patterson, this book Thrills!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2628967004897774756">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/30817744-sandy-the-world-could-end-while-i-was-reading-and-i-would-never-notice?shelf=4-star" class="actionLinkLite">4-star</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1255861381">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer484852291725596142">Audio.<br /><br />A really light easy read. It helps with audio versions when the chapters are short and pithy, as these definitely were.<br /><br />This book is the first in the Woman's Murder Club series.<br /><br />Inspector Lindsay Boxer of the San Francisco Police Department suddenly finds herself in the middle of two horrifying situations: The first is that she's just learned she has an often-fatal blood disease. The second is a double homicide case she is now heading up that involves the murder of newlyweds on their wedding</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText484852291725596142">Audio.<br /><br />A really light easy read. It helps with audio versions when the chapters are short and pithy, as these definitely were.<br /><br />This book is the first in the Woman's Murder Club series.<br /><br />Inspector Lindsay Boxer of the San Francisco Police Department suddenly finds herself in the middle of two horrifying situations: The first is that she's just learned she has an often-fatal blood disease. The second is a double homicide case she is now heading up that involves the murder of newlyweds on their wedding night. Burdened with Chris Raleigh, a new partner reassigned from the mayor's office, Lindsay finds that she has too much to deal with and turns to her best friend, Claire, the head ME on the case.<br /><br />With the help of fledgling newspaper reporter Cindy, and ADA Jill, Lindsay and Claire share private interdepartmental information in an effort to track and stop the killer before he strikes again.<br /><br />I wasn't expecting great things from this book, but I was pleasantly surprised and have already loaded the second in the series <a title="2nd Chance (Women's Murder Club, #2) by James Patterson" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13136.2nd_Chance__Women_s_Murder_Club___2_">2nd Chance</a> to listen to.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="484852291725596142">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_87402238">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87402238" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2917700-rebecca-t" class="left imgcol" title="Rebecca T"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1399454582p2/2917700.jpg" alt="Rebecca T" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/87402238?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 29, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2917700-rebecca-t" class="user" title="Rebecca T">Rebecca T</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13137.1st_to_Die" title="Paperback 9780446696616" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2917700-rebecca-t?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer87402238">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17322091424455781850">I really enjoyed "Women's Murder Club" back when it had its short stint on TV so I decided to give the book series a go. It took me a while to get my hands on the first book (because I refuse to read series' out of order) but I'm glad I made the effort.<br /><br />I found the murder scenes to be, and experience. I haven't read many crime novels, and the few I have read don't include the murderer's point of view as s/he's doing the murders. I found myself cringing over some of the details of the crimes and f</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17322091424455781850">I really enjoyed "Women's Murder Club" back when it had its short stint on TV so I decided to give the book series a go. It took me a while to get my hands on the first book (because I refuse to read series' out of order) but I'm glad I made the effort.<br /><br />I found the murder scenes to be, and experience. I haven't read many crime novels, and the few I have read don't include the murderer's point of view as s/he's doing the murders. I found myself cringing over some of the details of the crimes and found the killer's thoughts to be...well, psycho. <br /><br />I love the relationships in this book too. I found it interesting to see how each of the 'women' meet and how the club emerged. I also liked Lindsay's relationship with Chris. And can I just say I saw that little twist at the end coming, yet I still found it emotional.<br /><br />However, it lost points when Patterson opened up with Lindsay contemplating suicide, and then at the end that's glossed over. Lindsay dismissed the whole prologue in a single sentence. Also, I expected the writing to be better. James Patterson is an international bestseller so I expected his writing style to be of a higher quality.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17322091424455781850">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_421179566">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/421179566" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4635053-maria-jo-o-fernandes" class="left imgcol" title="Maria João Fernandes"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1452289570p2/4635053.jpg" alt="Maria João Fernandes" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/421179566?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 29, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4635053-maria-jo-o-fernandes" class="user" title="Maria João Fernandes">Maria João Fernandes</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/16044738-primeira-a-morrer" title="Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4635053-maria-jo-o-fernandes?shelf=own" class="actionLinkLite">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer421179566">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2494571896690937770">"Primeira a Morrer" é o primeiro livro da série "O Clube das Investigadoras" do James Patterson. Este thriller apresenta-nos a inspectora de homicídios, Lindsay Boxer e segue, detalhadamente, a sua vida pessoal e profissional. A presente investigação foca-se na procura de um assassino em série de recém-casados.<br /><br />Tive alguma dificuldade em relacionar-me com a protagonista. Apesar de o autor fazer uma descrição pormenorizada, sinto que, por vezes, o comportamento da mulher retratada é teatral, isto</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2494571896690937770">"Primeira a Morrer" é o primeiro livro da série "O Clube das Investigadoras" do James Patterson. Este thriller apresenta-nos a inspectora de homicídios, Lindsay Boxer e segue, detalhadamente, a sua vida pessoal e profissional. A presente investigação foca-se na procura de um assassino em série de recém-casados.<br /><br />Tive alguma dificuldade em relacionar-me com a protagonista. Apesar de o autor fazer uma descrição pormenorizada, sinto que, por vezes, o comportamento da mulher retratada é teatral, isto é, encenado. Não consigo imaginá-la como uma pessoa de verdade, no mundo real e este facto não me permitiu envolver e estabelecer uma ligação com o livro. <br /><br />Para além de Lindsay existem mais três membros no "Clube das Investigadoras": Claire, Cindy e Jill. Cada uma delas representa uma entidade diferente. O clube conta com uma investigadora, uma médica legista, uma jornalista e uma procuradora. A constituição do grupo promete uma junção de personalidades e vidas diferentes, contudo tal não é proporcionado ao leitor. James Patterson não desenvolve, neste primeiro livro, os pormenores relativos a cada uma das mulheres. Supostamente, estas três personagens desempenham um papel importante na vida de Linsay e, acima de tudo, têm um influência enorme na resolução do crime em questão. Contudo, as suas histórias e pensamentos são regalados para segundo plano.<br /><br />Apesar de o livro ser produto de uma mente masculina, senti que o autor tenta provar que as mulheres são capazes de resolver um mistério, sem a ajuda de um homem. Apesar disso e, como não podia deixar de ser, o sexo masculino é um tema debatido pelas quatro amigas. <br /><br />Inicialmente, esta obra cativou-me bastante. Contudo, à medida que a história avançou e determinados detalhes me foram desvendados, senti a desilusão apoderar-se de mim. Os acontecimentos revelaram-se previsíveis, os diálogos cansativos e o desfecho decepcionante.<br /><br />Apesar de terem sido poucas as surpresas do enredo e o fio condutor principal se revelar simples e pouco criativo foi uma leitura interessante. É um bom livro para quem deseja ler algo leve, que não exiga concentração ou especial atenção. Uma boa forma de descontrair ou fazer uma pausa em leituras mais exigentes.<br /><br />É sempre difícil para mim gostar verdadeiramente de um livro cujas personagens mantêm uma distância considerável do meu mundo. Contudo, como está divido em muitos capítulos e a escrita é bastante simples, o ritmo é muito rápido e o livro lê-se num instante. <br /><br />Do James Patterson apenas ainda tinha lido "A Noiva Assassina" e esse vale a pena o investimento.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2494571896690937770">...more</a>

          </span>
