    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_297209202">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/297209202" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3816725-larry-bassett" class="left imgcol" title="Larry Bassett"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1390874855p2/3816725.jpg" alt="Larry Bassett" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/297209202?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 30, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3816725-larry-bassett" class="user" title="Larry Bassett">Larry Bassett</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13137.1st_to_Die" title="Paperback 9780446696616" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3816725-larry-bassett?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer297209202">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6227746660924187448">How long has it been since you have stayed up too late to finish a book that you just couldn’t put down? It happened to be last night and the book was <em>First to Die</em> by <a title="James Patterson" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3780.James_Patterson">James Patterson</a>. I was surprised because I thought Patterson was an author who produced books off an assembly line. <br /><br />I love a book with short chapters. It fits my attention span. None of that wondering how many pages until the end of the chapter so I can go see if I have any email or to have just one (more) cookie. This book fits th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6227746660924187448">How long has it been since you have stayed up too late to finish a book that you just couldn’t put down? It happened to be last night and the book was <em>First to Die</em> by <a title="James Patterson" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3780.James_Patterson">James Patterson</a>. I was surprised because I thought Patterson was an author who produced books off an assembly line. <br /><br />I love a book with short chapters. It fits my attention span. None of that wondering how many pages until the end of the chapter so I can go see if I have any email or to have just one (more) cookie. This book fits that mold nicely. <br /><br />First impression: The police making jokes as they view the bodies of the bride and groom in their hotel suite still dressed in their wedding attire: “Guess things went downhill for them quicker than most.” Seems a little tasteless or maybe it is the way all Patterson mystery novels begin. Maybe it is the author saying “Don’t take this book too seriously.” Or maybe it’s just Jacobi’s job to be the crude cop. But it turns out that Jabobi, the partner of our protagonist, is pretty quickly relegated to a secondary role. <br /><br />What do I know about James Patterson? He and his co-authors have written a lot of books. This is the first in the Women’s Murder Club series. Patterson could retire on his book earnings, and maybe he has. Maybe that is why he has turned over some of his writing to clones. This is my first Patterson mystery. If I had known that his name is just a front for his writing corporation, I would not have several more of his books on my TBR shelf. But I have a mantra: You bought these books. Now, read them! I got them cheap but maybe I overpaid. This book is from 2001 and maybe he was still a fresh writer then. I won’t know that until I sample a couple more of his books. <br /><br />First books in a series are in demand by people like me. I am introduced to the main characters who I will encounter as I move further into the series. The series might have been published years ago but I still get to start fresh as I begin at the beginning. I am new to mysteries, having left them decades ago when I grew out of the Hardy Boys series. I decided I was focused way too much on non-fiction and I had to have more fun reading. So I decided to try out some mysteries with strong women protagonists. Once I got into selecting books I found out how very many NY Times Best Selling Authors of mysteries there are. I might have bit off more than I wanted. Will I like Inspector Lindsey Boxer as much as I like V.I. Warshawski? Or hate her as much as I hate Stephanie Plum?<br /><br />Maxine Paetro has collaborated with James Patterson to write the Women’s Murder Club series beginning with <a title="1st to Die (Women's Murder Club, #1) by James Patterson" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13137.1st_to_Die__Women_s_Murder_Club___1_"> The Fourth of July </a>. This link takes you to some information about her: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://freshfiction.com/page.php?id=1904" target="_blank">http://freshfiction.com/page.php?id=1904</a> . Although this is a bit of a puff piece, it does tell how the authors met in the New York advertising world. Paetro, a new woman author for me, didn’t collaborate with Patterson until the fourth book in this series. But I wanted to start with number one and will be paying attention to see if I notice any difference when the collaboration begins.<br /><br />Having read only this one book by Patterson, I do not know if he has a run of the mill or unique template for his stories or a template at all for that matter. I don’t know if he has a predictable pattern in his books but his consortium of writers sure do crank them out and they are at the top of the earnings and popularity charts. But, as a relatively inexperienced mystery reader, I did enjoy reading this book quite a lot. It has enough complexity and mystery and dramatic tension for me. His mass market paperbacks are shouting at you from the grocery store racks so a lot of regular people must buy them. There was enough intellectual and emotional stimulation without overshooting its mass audience target. It did not challenge my intellect and that is just the way I wanted it. I have not enjoyed or appreciated more than several books that have won big awards. With the book I liked not having to figure out the symbols and the meanings. Just a good enjoyable read. <br /><br />However Patterson has some failings. The Woman’s Murder Club is populated by women so there should be, I think, a good deal of sensitivity to women’s issues. And there is a good heavy dose of strong women here. <br /><blockquote> We looked around the table. We were bright, attractive, take-no-shit women. We were going to run things – some day. </blockquote><br />I also wouldn’t mind some feminist attributes more than good humored man hating. <br /><blockquote> That man was standing there in his suit with a two-inch dick. </blockquote> <br />I don’t think from this limited exposure to Patterson that he fairs so well at being a feminist. His female lead character Lindsay has a sexually charged relationship with her male work partner and he fails to survive the “No Means No” test. He pressures, she resists, he pressures more, she still resists, he pressures yet again, and she finally gives in and then is happy she succumbed. This is the She Really Wanted It Even Though She Resisted false truism. <br /><blockquote> Now she was loving it, as she always did. It wasn’t bad – it was good. They all ended up wanting it and loving it. He always picked them so well. </blockquote><br />This is a mass market author so hoping for a book that would please a feminist was only a faint hope at best. But the book was quite a bit better than mediocre and the drinking was mostly wine rather than scotch. And, could it be? There was no smoking or did I just miss it? That would be a milestone in my experience.<br /><br />I will read more of the Women’s Murder Club series so I can judge it better. There is definitely room for improvement and I wonder if a woman writing collaborator will make a difference. The next book on my shelf from the series is #4 when Maxine Paetro makes her debut. I am giving <em>First to Die</em> three and a half stars rounded up to four to indicate my optimistic hope for improvement from the strong women perspective. <br /><br />I am pleasantly surprised by how much I liked this book. I am not sure whether than says more about me or the book. And I have not read Patterson books outside of this series to know if this is just filling the strong women niche while his macho, smoking, whiskey drinking men are in some other series.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6227746660924187448">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/159895936?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 09, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4816194-debra" class="user" title="Debra">Debra</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13137.1st_to_Die" title="Paperback 9780446696616" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4816194-debra?shelf=series" class="actionLinkLite">series</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4816194-debra?shelf=mystery-thriller" class="actionLinkLite">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer159895936">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9656100298391723205">I guess I'm just about pooped out with Patterson's novels. I kept up with Alex Cross for a long time, but I finally stopped picking up the next book. Unique when he first started his Alex Cross books, his writing just now seems a rehash of similar characters in similar circumstances. The same is for the new 4-gals-team-up-and-solve-murders series... same ole' same ole' for me. My bad, I sound so negative. Sorry folks. <br /><br />Any of Patterson's books are great for light, easy, and FAST reads; although s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9656100298391723205">I guess I'm just about pooped out with Patterson's novels. I kept up with Alex Cross for a long time, but I finally stopped picking up the next book. Unique when he first started his Alex Cross books, his writing just now seems a rehash of similar characters in similar circumstances. The same is for the new 4-gals-team-up-and-solve-murders series... same ole' same ole' for me. My bad, I sound so negative. Sorry folks. <br /><br />Any of Patterson's books are great for light, easy, and FAST reads; although some may not be too great for the squeamish as he puts in a lot of gruesome details about murder victims; <a title="Kiss the Girls (Alex Cross, #2) by James Patterson" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13148.Kiss_the_Girls__Alex_Cross___2_">Kiss the Girls</a> comes to mind here (which I thought was a pretty good read). <br /><br />Anyway, I hate to come down on Patterson, but it's time for me to move on. So many books, so little time.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9656100298391723205">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1650769-olivia?shelf=audiobook" class="actionLinkLite">audiobook</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1357625905">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5393688688599779395">Embarrassing to say because it is Patterson but, good book for what it is! A very fast read, a good thriller with a twist that though you can see coming was still fun to read. I didn't expect it to be so graphic though, and I didn't foresee the heavy romance. Odd. Either way, a summer thriller with a CSI/Criminal Minds feel to it. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

That\'s w&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText18348093423168984402\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;See alternate cover edition here\n\nVirginia Medical Examiner Kay Scarpetta has a bloody puzzle on her hands: five headless, limbless cadavers in Ireland, plus four similar victims in a landfill back home. Is a serial butcher loose in Virginia? That\'s what the panicked public thinks, thanks to a local TV reporter who got the leaked news from her boyfriend, Scarpetta\'s vile rival, Investigator Percy Ring. But the butchered bodies are so many red herrings intended to throw idiots like Ring off the track. Instead of a run-of-the-mill serial killer, we\'re dealing with a shadowy figure who has plans involving mutant smallpox, mass murder, and messing with Scarpetta\'s mind by e-mailing her gory photos of the murder scenes, along with cryptic AOL chat-room messages. The coolest innovation: Scarpetta\'s gorgeous genius niece, Lucy, equips her with a DataGlove and a VPL Eyephone, and she takes a creepy virtual tour of the e-mailed crime scene.\n\nUnnatural Exposure boasts brisk storytelling, crackling dialogue, evocative prose about forensic-science sleuthing, and crisp character sketches, both of familiar characters like Scarpetta\'s gruff partner Pete Marino and bit players like the landfill employee falsely accused by Ring. Plus, let\'s face it: serial killers are old hat. Cornwell\'s most vivid villains are highly plausible backstabbing colleagues like Ring, who plots to destroy Lucy\'s FBI career by outing her as a lesbian. Some readers object to the rather abrupt ending, but, hey, it\'s less jarring than Hannibal\'s, and it\'s the logical culmination of Cornwell\'s philosophy about human nature. To illuminate the novel\'s finale, read Cornwell\'s remarks on paranoia in her Amazon.com interview. --Tim Appelo&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a data-text-id=\"18348093423168984402\" href=\"#\"     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3780.James_Patterson">About James Patterson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/3780.James_Patterson"><img alt="3780" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1284492096p2/3780.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer6909725449015268188"><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespatterson.com">Offical US Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk">Offical UK Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespattersonya.com">Offical James Patterson Young Adult Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.middleschoolbook.com">Offical Site for James Patterson's Middle School Series</a><br /><br /><br /><br />The subject of a <em>Time</em> magazine feature called, "The Man Who Can't Miss," James Patterson is the bestselling author of the past year, bar none, with more than 16 million books sold in North America alone. In 2007, one of every fifteen hardcover fiction books sold was a Patter</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6909725449015268188"><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespatterson.com">Offical US Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk">Offical UK Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespattersonya.com">Offical James Patterson Young Adult Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.middleschoolbook.com">Offical Site for James Patterson's Middle School Series</a><br /><br /><br /><br />The subject of a <em>Time</em> magazine feature called, "The Man Who Can't Miss," James Patterson is the bestselling author of the past year, bar none, with more than 16 million books sold in North America alone. In 2007, one of every fifteen hardcover fiction books sold was a Patterson title. In the past three years, James has sold more books than any other author (according to Bookscan), and in total, James's books have sold an estimated 220 million copies worldwide. He is the first author to have #1 new titles simultaneously on <em>The New York Times</em> adult and children's lists and is the only author to have five new hardcover novels debut at #1 on the list in one year—a record-breaking feat he's accomplished every year since 2005. To date, James Patterson has had nineteen consecutive #1 <em>New York Times</em> bestselling novels, and holds the <em>New York Times</em> record for most Hardcover Fiction bestselling titles by a single author (63 total), which is also a Guinness World Record.<br /><br /><br /><br />From his James Patterson Pageturner Awards (which rewarded groups and individuals for creative and effective ways to spread the joy of reading) to his website <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.readkiddoread.com">ReadKiddoRead.com</a> (which helps adults find books that kids are sure to love) to his regular donations of thousands of books to troops overseas, Patterson is a lifelong champion of books and reading. His first foray into books for all ages was the critically acclaimed Maximum Ride series, which debuted on the New York Times bestsellers list at #1 and remained there for twelve straight weeks. The series has so far made appearances on <em>The New York Times</em> bestsellers lists ninety-four cumulative times, proving that kids of all ages love page turners. He captured the attention of boy readers with the Daniel X series, and his third series for readers of all ages debuted in December 2009 with <em>Witch &amp; Wizard</em>, which spent five consecutive weeks atop the <em>New York Times</em> bestsellers list.<br /><br /><br /><br />Patterson is the creator of the #1 new detective series of the past dozen years, featuring Alex Cross and including the Hollywood-adapted "Along Came a Spider" and "Kiss the Girls," starring Academy Award-winning actor Morgan Freeman. He is also the creator of the #1 new detective series of the past five years, featuring Lindsay Boxer and the other members of the Women's Murder Club, from which the ABC television drama series was adapted. He has authored books behind six films on the Hollywood fast-track, including the upcoming Maximum Ride movie forthcoming from Avi Arad, the producer of X-Men and Spiderman.<br /><br /><br /><br />He is the author of novels—from The Thomas Berryman Number (1976) to Honeymoon (2005)—that have won awards including the Edgar, the BCA Mystery Guild's Thriller of the Year, the International Thriller of the Year award, and the Reader's Digest Reader's Choice Award. And, he has won a Children's Choice Book Council's Children's Choice Awards "Author of the Year" award (2010).<br /><br /><br /><br />One of Forbes magazine's Celebrity 100, James made a guest appearance on the popular FOX TV show "The Simpsons" in March, 2007.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6909725449015268188">...more</a>

    </div>
